       1             : /* stb_image - v2.14 - public domain image loader -
       2             : http://nothings.org/stb_image.h no warranty implied; use at your own risk
       3             : 
       4             : Do this:
       5             : #define STB_IMAGE_IMPLEMENTATION
       6             : before you include this file in *one* C or C++ file to create the
       7             : implementation.
       8             : 
       9             : // i.e. it should look like this:
      10             : #include ...
      11             : #include ...
      12             : #include ...
      13             : #define STB_IMAGE_IMPLEMENTATION
      14             : #include "stb_image.h"
      15             : 
      16             : You can #define STBI_ASSERT(x) before the #include to avoid using assert.h.
      17             : And #define STBI_MALLOC, STBI_REALLOC, and STBI_FREE to avoid using
      18             : malloc,realloc,free
      19             : 
      20             : 
      21             : QUICK NOTES:
      22             : Primarily of interest to game developers and other people who can
      23             : avoid problematic images and only need the trivial interface
      24             : 
      25             : JPEG baseline & progressive (12 bpc/arithmetic not supported, same as stock IJG
      26             : lib) PNG 1/2/4/8-bit-per-channel (16 bpc not supported)
      27             : 
      28             : TGA (not sure what subset, if a subset)
      29             : BMP non-1bpp, non-RLE
      30             : PSD (composited view only, no extra channels, 8/16 bit-per-channel)
      31             : 
      32             : GIF (*comp always reports as 4-channel)
      33             : HDR (radiance rgbE format)
      34             : PIC (Softimage PIC)
      35             : PNM (PPM and PGM binary only)
      36             : 
      37             : Animated GIF still needs a proper API, but here's one way to do it:
      38             : http://gist.github.com/urraka/685d9a6340b26b830d49
      39             : 
      40             : - decode from memory or through FILE (define STBI_NO_STDIO to remove code)
      41             : - decode from arbitrary I/O callbacks
      42             : - SIMD acceleration on x86/x64 (SSE2) and ARM (NEON)
      43             : 
      44             : Full documentation under "DOCUMENTATION" below.
      45             : 
      46             : 
      47             : Revision 2.00 release notes:
      48             : 
      49             : - Progressive JPEG is now supported.
      50             : 
      51             : - PPM and PGM binary formats are now supported, thanks to Ken Miller.
      52             : 
      53             : - x86 platforms now make use of SSE2 SIMD instructions for
      54             : JPEG decoding, and ARM platforms can use NEON SIMD if requested.
      55             : This work was done by Fabian "ryg" Giesen. SSE2 is used by
      56             : default, but NEON must be enabled explicitly; see docs.
      57             : 
      58             : With other JPEG optimizations included in this version, we see
      59             : 2x speedup on a JPEG on an x86 machine, and a 1.5x speedup
      60             : on a JPEG on an ARM machine, relative to previous versions of this
      61             : library. The same results will not obtain for all JPGs and for all
      62             : x86/ARM machines. (Note that progressive JPEGs are significantly
      63             : slower to decode than regular JPEGs.) This doesn't mean that this
      64             : is the fastest JPEG decoder in the land; rather, it brings it
      65             : closer to parity with standard libraries. If you want the fastest
      66             : decode, look elsewhere. (See "Philosophy" section of docs below.)
      67             : 
      68             : See final bullet items below for more info on SIMD.
      69             : 
      70             : - Added STBI_MALLOC, STBI_REALLOC, and STBI_FREE macros for replacing
      71             : the memory allocator. Unlike other STBI libraries, these macros don't
      72             : support a context parameter, so if you need to pass a context in to
      73             : the allocator, you'll have to store it in a global or a thread-local
      74             : variable.
      75             : 
      76             : - Split existing STBI_NO_HDR flag into two flags, STBI_NO_HDR and
      77             : STBI_NO_LINEAR.
      78             : STBI_NO_HDR:     suppress implementation of .hdr reader format
      79             : STBI_NO_LINEAR:  suppress high-dynamic-range light-linear float API
      80             : 
      81             : - You can suppress implementation of any of the decoders to reduce
      82             : your code footprint by #defining one or more of the following
      83             : symbols before creating the implementation.
      84             : 
      85             : STBI_NO_JPEG
      86             : STBI_NO_PNG
      87             : STBI_NO_BMP
      88             : STBI_NO_PSD
      89             : STBI_NO_TGA
      90             : STBI_NO_GIF
      91             : STBI_NO_HDR
      92             : STBI_NO_PIC
      93             : STBI_NO_PNM   (.ppm and .pgm)
      94             : 
      95             : - You can request *only* certain decoders and suppress all other ones
      96             : (this will be more forward-compatible, as addition of new decoders
      97             : doesn't require you to disable them explicitly):
      98             : 
      99             : STBI_ONLY_JPEG
     100             : STBI_ONLY_PNG
     101             : STBI_ONLY_BMP
     102             : STBI_ONLY_PSD
     103             : STBI_ONLY_TGA
     104             : STBI_ONLY_GIF
     105             : STBI_ONLY_HDR
     106             : STBI_ONLY_PIC
     107             : STBI_ONLY_PNM   (.ppm and .pgm)
     108             : 
     109             : Note that you can define multiples of these, and you will get all
     110             : of them ("only x" and "only y" is interpreted to mean "only x&y").
     111             : 
     112             : - If you use STBI_NO_PNG (or _ONLY_ without PNG), and you still
     113             : want the zlib decoder to be available, #define STBI_SUPPORT_ZLIB
     114             : 
     115             : - Compilation of all SIMD code can be suppressed with
     116             : #define STBI_NO_SIMD
     117             : It should not be necessary to disable SIMD unless you have issues
     118             : compiling (e.g. using an x86 compiler which doesn't support SSE
     119             : intrinsics or that doesn't support the method used to detect
     120             : SSE2 support at run-time), and even those can be reported as
     121             : bugs so I can refine the built-in compile-time checking to be
     122             : smarter.
     123             : 
     124             : - The old STBI_SIMD system which allowed installing a user-defined
     125             : IDCT etc. has been removed. If you need this, don't upgrade. My
     126             : assumption is that almost nobody was doing this, and those who
     127             : were will find the built-in SIMD more satisfactory anyway.
     128             : 
     129             : - RGB values computed for JPEG images are slightly different from
     130             : previous versions of stb_image. (This is due to using less
     131             : integer precision in SIMD.) The C code has been adjusted so
     132             : that the same RGB values will be computed regardless of whether
     133             : SIMD support is available, so your app should always produce
     134             : consistent results. But these results are slightly different from
     135             : previous versions. (Specifically, about 3% of available YCbCr values
     136             : will compute different RGB results from pre-1.49 versions by +-1;
     137             : most of the deviating values are one smaller in the G channel.)
     138             : 
     139             : - If you must produce consistent results with previous versions of
     140             : stb_image, #define STBI_JPEG_OLD and you will get the same results
     141             : you used to; however, you will not get the SIMD speedups for
     142             : the YCbCr-to-RGB conversion step (although you should still see
     143             : significant JPEG speedup from the other changes).
     144             : 
     145             : Please note that STBI_JPEG_OLD is a temporary feature; it will be
     146             : removed in future versions of the library. It is only intended for
     147             : near-term back-compatibility use.
     148             : 
     149             : 
     150             : Latest revision history:
     151             : 2.13  (2016-12-04) experimental 16-bit API, only for PNG so far; fixes
     152             : 2.12  (2016-04-02) fix typo in 2.11 PSD fix that caused crashes
     153             : 2.11  (2016-04-02) 16-bit PNGS; enable SSE2 in non-gcc x64
     154             : RGB-format JPEG; remove white matting in PSD;
     155             : allocate large structures on the stack;
     156             : correct channel count for PNG & BMP
     157             : 2.10  (2016-01-22) avoid warning introduced in 2.09
     158             : 2.09  (2016-01-16) 16-bit TGA; comments in PNM files; STBI_REALLOC_SIZED
     159             : 2.08  (2015-09-13) fix to 2.07 cleanup, reading RGB PSD as RGBA
     160             : 2.07  (2015-09-13) partial animated GIF support
     161             : limited 16-bit PSD support
     162             : minor bugs, code cleanup, and compiler warnings
     163             : 
     164             : See end of file for full revision history.
     165             : 
     166             :

     206             : */
     207             : #ifndef STBI_INCLUDE_STB_IMAGE_H
     208             : #define STBI_INCLUDE_STB_IMAGE_H
     209             : 
     210             : // DOCUMENTATION
     211             : //
     212             : // Limitations:
     213             : //    - no 16-bit-per-channel PNG
     214             : //    - no 12-bit-per-channel JPEG
     215             : //    - no JPEGs with arithmetic coding
     216             : //    - no 1-bit BMP
     217             : //    - GIF always returns *comp=4
     218             : //
     219             : // Basic usage (see HDR discussion below for HDR usage):
     220             : //    int x,y,n;
     221             : //    unsigned char *data = stbi_load(filename, &x, &y, &n, 0);
     222             : //    // ... process data if not NULL ...
     223             : //    // ... x = width, y = height, n = # 8-bit components per pixel ...
     224             : //    // ... replace '0' with '1'..'4' to force that many components per pixel
     225             : //    // ... but 'n' will always be the number that it would have been if you
     226             : //    said 0 stbi_image_free(data)
     227             : //
     228             : // Standard parameters:
     229             : //    int *x                 -- outputs image width in pixels
     230             : //    int *y                 -- outputs image height in pixels
     231             : //    int *channels_in_file  -- outputs # of image components in image file
     232             : //    int desired_channels   -- if non-zero, # of image components requested in
     233             : //    result
     234             : //
     235             : // The return value from an image loader is an 'unsigned char *' which points
     236             : // to the pixel data, or NULL on an allocation failure or if the image is
     237             : // corrupt or invalid. The pixel data consists of *y scanlines of *x pixels,
     238             : // with each pixel consisting of N interleaved 8-bit components; the first
     239             : // pixel pointed to is top-left-most in the image. There is no padding between
     240             : // image scanlines or between pixels, regardless of format. The number of
     241             : // components N is 'req_comp' if req_comp is non-zero, or *comp otherwise.
     242             : // If req_comp is non-zero, *comp has the number of components that _would_
     243             : // have been output otherwise. E.g. if you set req_comp to 4, you will always
     244             : // get RGBA output, but you can check *comp to see if it's trivially opaque
     245             : // because e.g. there were only 3 channels in the source image.
     246             : //
     247             : // An output image with N components has the following components interleaved
     248             : // in this order in each pixel:
     249             : //
     250             : //     N=#comp     components
     251             : //       1           grey
     252             : //       2           grey, alpha
     253             : //       3           red, green, blue
     254             : //       4           red, green, blue, alpha
     255             : //
     256             : // If image loading fails for any reason, the return value will be NULL,
     257             : // and *x, *y, *comp will be unchanged. The function stbi_failure_reason()
     258             : // can be queried for an extremely brief, end-user unfriendly explanation
     259             : // of why the load failed. Define STBI_NO_FAILURE_STRINGS to avoid
     260             : // compiling these strings at all, and STBI_FAILURE_USERMSG to get slightly
     261             : // more user-friendly ones.
     262             : //
     263             : // Paletted PNG, BMP, GIF, and PIC images are automatically depalettized.
     264             : //
     265             : // ===========================================================================
     266             : //
     267             : // Philosophy
     268             : //
     269             : // stb libraries are designed with the following priorities:
     270             : //
     271             : //    1. easy to use
     272             : //    2. easy to maintain
     273             : //    3. good performance
     274             : //
     275             : // Sometimes I let "good performance" creep up in priority over "easy to
     276             : // maintain", and for best performance I may provide less-easy-to-use APIs that
     277             : // give higher performance, in addition to the easy to use ones. Nevertheless,
     278             : // it's important to keep in mind that from the standpoint of you, a client of
     279             : // this library, all you care about is #1 and #3, and stb libraries do not
     280             : // emphasize #3 above all.
     281             : //
     282             : // Some secondary priorities arise directly from the first two, some of which
     283             : // make more explicit reasons why performance can't be emphasized.
     284             : //
     285             : //    - Portable ("ease of use")
     286             : //    - Small footprint ("easy to maintain")
     287             : //    - No dependencies ("ease of use")
     288             : //
     289             : // ===========================================================================
     290             : //
     291             : // I/O callbacks
     292             : //
     293             : // I/O callbacks allow you to read from arbitrary sources, like packaged
     294             : // files or some other source. Data read from callbacks are processed
     295             : // through a small internal buffer (currently 128 bytes) to try to reduce
     296             : // overhead.
     297             : //
     298             : // The three functions you must define are "read" (reads some bytes of data),
     299             : // "skip" (skips some bytes of data), "eof" (reports if the stream is at the
     300             : // end).
     301             : //
     302             : // ===========================================================================
     303             : //
     304             : // SIMD support
     305             : //
     306             : // The JPEG decoder will try to automatically use SIMD kernels on x86 when
     307             : // supported by the compiler. For ARM Neon support, you must explicitly
     308             : // request it.
     309             : //
     310             : // (The old do-it-yourself SIMD API is no longer supported in the current
     311             : // code.)
     312             : //
     313             : // On x86, SSE2 will automatically be used when available based on a run-time
     314             : // test; if not, the generic C versions are used as a fall-back. On ARM targets,
     315             : // the typical path is to have separate builds for NEON and non-NEON devices
     316             : // (at least this is true for iOS and Android). Therefore, the NEON support is
     317             : // toggled by a build flag: define STBI_NEON to get NEON loops.
     318             : //
     319             : // The output of the JPEG decoder is slightly different from versions where
     320             : // SIMD support was introduced (that is, for versions before 1.49). The
     321             : // difference is only +-1 in the 8-bit RGB channels, and only on a small
     322             : // fraction of pixels. You can force the pre-1.49 behavior by defining
     323             : // STBI_JPEG_OLD, but this will disable some of the SIMD decoding path
     324             : // and hence cost some performance.
     325             : //
     326             : // If for some reason you do not want to use any of SIMD code, or if
     327             : // you have issues compiling it, you can disable it entirely by
     328             : // defining STBI_NO_SIMD.
     329             : //
     330             : // ===========================================================================
     331             : //
     332             : // HDR image support   (disable by defining STBI_NO_HDR)
     333             : //
     334             : // stb_image now supports loading HDR images in general, and currently
     335             : // the Radiance .HDR file format, although the support is provided
     336             : // generically. You can still load any file through the existing interface;
     337             : // if you attempt to load an HDR file, it will be automatically remapped to
     338             : // LDR, assuming gamma 2.2 and an arbitrary scale factor defaulting to 1;
     339             : // both of these constants can be reconfigured through this interface:
     340             : //
     341             : //     stbi_hdr_to_ldr_gamma(2.2f);
     342             : //     stbi_hdr_to_ldr_scale(1.0f);
     343             : //
     344             : // (note, do not use _inverse_ constants; stbi_image will invert them
     345             : // appropriately).
     346             : //
     347             : // Additionally, there is a new, parallel interface for loading files as
     348             : // (linear) floats to preserve the full dynamic range:
     349             : //
     350             : //    float *data = stbi_loadf(filename, &x, &y, &n, 0);
     351             : //
     352             : // If you load LDR images through this interface, those images will
     353             : // be promoted to floating point values, run through the inverse of
     354             : // constants corresponding to the above:
     355             : //
     356             : //     stbi_ldr_to_hdr_scale(1.0f);
     357             : //     stbi_ldr_to_hdr_gamma(2.2f);
     358             : //
     359             : // Finally, given a filename (or an open file or memory block--see header
     360             : // file for details) containing image data, you can query for the "most
     361             : // appropriate" interface to use (that is, whether the image is HDR or
     362             : // not), using:
     363             : //
     364             : //     stbi_is_hdr(char *filename);
     365             : //
     366             : // ===========================================================================
     367             : //
     368             : // iPhone PNG support:
     369             : //
     370             : // By default we convert iphone-formatted PNGs back to RGB, even though
     371             : // they are internally encoded differently. You can disable this conversion
     372             : // by by calling stbi_convert_iphone_png_to_rgb(0), in which case
     373             : // you will always just get the native iphone "format" through (which
     374             : // is BGR stored in RGB).
     375             : //
     376             : // Call stbi_set_unpremultiply_on_load(1) as well to force a divide per
     377             : // pixel to remove any premultiplied alpha *only* if the image file explicitly
     378             : // says there's premultiplied data (currently only happens in iPhone images,
     379             : // and only if iPhone convert-to-rgb processing is on).
     380             : //
     381             : 
     382             : 
     383             : #ifndef STBI_NO_STDIO
     384             : #include <stdio.h>
     385             : #endif // STBI_NO_STDIO
     386             : 
     387             : #define STBI_VERSION 1
     388             : 
     389             : enum {
     390             :   STBI_default = 0, // only used for req_comp
     391             : 
     392             :   STBI_grey = 1,
     393             :   STBI_grey_alpha = 2,
     394             :   STBI_rgb = 3,
     395             :   STBI_rgb_alpha = 4
     396             : };
     397             : 
     398             : typedef unsigned char stbi_uc;
     399             : typedef unsigned short stbi_us;
     400             : 
     401             : #ifdef __cplusplus
     402             : extern "C" {
     403             : #endif
     404             : 
     405             : #ifdef STB_IMAGE_STATIC
     406             : #define STBIDEF static
     407             : #else
     408             : #define STBIDEF extern
     409             : #endif
     410             : 
     411             : //////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
     412             : //
     413             : // PRIMARY API - works on images of any type
     414             : //
     415             : 
     416             : //
     417             : // load image by filename, open file, or memory buffer
     418             : //
     419             : 
     420             : typedef struct {
     421             :   int (*read)(void *user, char *data,
     422             :               int size); // fill 'data' with 'size' bytes.  return number of
     423             :                          // bytes actually read
     424             :   void (*skip)(void *user, int n); // skip the next 'n' bytes, or 'unget' the
     425             :                                    // last -n bytes if negative
     426             :   int (*eof)(void *user); // returns nonzero if we are at end of file/data
     427             : } stbi_io_callbacks;
     428             : 
     429             : ////////////////////////////////////
     430             : //
     431             : // 8-bits-per-channel interface
     432             : //
     433             : 
     434             : STBIDEF stbi_uc *
     435             : stbi_load(char const *filename, int *x, int *y, int *channels_in_file,
     436             :           int desired_channels);
     437             : STBIDEF stbi_uc *
     438             : stbi_load_from_memory(stbi_uc const *buffer, int len, int *x, int *y,
     439             :                       int *channels_in_file, int desired_channels);
     440             : STBIDEF stbi_uc *
     441             : stbi_load_from_callbacks(stbi_io_callbacks const *clbk, void *user, int *x,
     442             :                          int *y, int *channels_in_file, int desired_channels);
     443             : 
     444             : #ifndef STBI_NO_STDIO
     445             : STBIDEF stbi_uc *
     446             : stbi_load_from_file(FILE *f, int *x, int *y, int *channels_in_file,
     447             :                     int desired_channels);
     448             : // for stbi_load_from_file, file pointer is left pointing immediately after
     449             : // image
     450             : #endif
     451             : 
     452             : ////////////////////////////////////
     453             : //
     454             : // 16-bits-per-channel interface
     455             : //
     456             : 
     457             : STBIDEF stbi_us *
     458             : stbi_load_16(char const *filename, int *x, int *y, int *channels_in_file,
     459             :              int desired_channels);
     460             : #ifndef STBI_NO_STDIO
     461             : STBIDEF stbi_us *
     462             : stbi_load_from_file_16(FILE *f, int *x, int *y, int *channels_in_file,
     463             :                        int desired_channels);
     464             : #endif
     465             : // @TODO the other variants
     466             : 
     467             : ////////////////////////////////////
     468             : //
     469             : // float-per-channel interface
     470             : //
     471             : #ifndef STBI_NO_LINEAR
     472             : STBIDEF float *
     473             : stbi_loadf(char const *filename, int *x, int *y, int *channels_in_file,
     474             :            int desired_channels);
     475             : STBIDEF float *
     476             : stbi_loadf_from_memory(stbi_uc const *buffer, int len, int *x, int *y,
     477             :                        int *channels_in_file, int desired_channels);
     478             : STBIDEF float *
     479             : stbi_loadf_from_callbacks(stbi_io_callbacks const *clbk, void *user, int *x,
     480             :                           int *y, int *channels_in_file, int desired_channels);
     481             : 
     482             : #ifndef STBI_NO_STDIO
     483             : STBIDEF float *
     484             : stbi_loadf_from_file(FILE *f, int *x, int *y, int *channels_in_file,
     485             :                      int desired_channels);
     486             : #endif
     487             : #endif
     488             : 
     489             : #ifndef STBI_NO_HDR
     490             : STBIDEF void
     491             : stbi_hdr_to_ldr_gamma(float gamma);
     492             : STBIDEF void
     493             : stbi_hdr_to_ldr_scale(float scale);
     494             : #endif // STBI_NO_HDR
     495             : 
     496             : #ifndef STBI_NO_LINEAR
     497             : STBIDEF void
     498             : stbi_ldr_to_hdr_gamma(float gamma);
     499             : STBIDEF void
     500             : stbi_ldr_to_hdr_scale(float scale);

     725             : // gcc doesn't support sse2 intrinsics unless you compile with -msse2,
     726             : // (but compiling with -msse2 allows the compiler to use SSE2 everywhere;
     727             : // this is just broken and gcc are jerks for not fixing it properly
     728             : // http://www.virtualdub.org/blog/pivot/entry.php?id=363 )

     734             : // Note that __MINGW32__ doesn't actually mean 32-bit, so we have to avoid
     735             : // STBI__X64_TARGET
     736             : //
     737             : // 32-bit MinGW wants ESP to be 16-byte aligned, but this is not in the
     738             : // Windows ABI and VC++ as well as Windows DLLs don't maintain that invariant.
     739             : // As a result, enabling SSE2 on 32-bit MinGW is dangerous when not
     740             : // simultaneously enabling "-mstackrealign".
     741             : //
     742             : // See https://github.com/nothings/stb/issues/81 for more information.
     743             : //
     744             : // So default to no SSE2 on 32-bit MinGW. If you've read this far and added
     745             : // -mstackrealign to your build settings, feel free to #define
     746             : // STBI_MINGW_ENABLE_SSE2.

    1036             : 
    1037             : // stb_image uses ints pervasively, including for offset calculations.
    1038             : // therefore the largest decoded image size we can support with the
    1039             : // current code, even on 64-bit targets, is INT_MAX. this is not a
    1040             : // significant limitation for the intended use case.
    1041             : //
    1042             : // we do, however, need to make sure our size calculations don't
    1043             : // overflow. hence a few helper functions for size calculations that

    1998             : //  "baseline" JPEG/JFIF decoder
    1999             : //
    2000             : //    simple implementation
    2001             : //      - doesn't support delayed output of y-dimension
    2002             : //      - simple interface (only one output format: 8-bit interleaved RGB)
    2003             : //      - doesn't try to recover corrupt jpegs
    2004             : //      - doesn't allow partial loading, loading multiple at once
    2005             : //      - still fast on x86 (copying globals into locals doesn't help x86)
    2006             : //      - allocates lots of intermediate memory (full size of all components)
    2007             : //        - non-interleaved case requires this anyway
    2008             : //        - allows good upsampling (see next)
    2009             : //    high-quality
    2010             : //      - upsampled channels are bilinearly interpolated, even across blocks
    2011             : //      - quality integer IDCT derived from IJG's 'slow'
    2012             : //    performance
    2013             : //      - fast huffman; reasonable integer IDCT
    2014             : //      - some SIMD kernels for common paths on targets with SSE2/NEON
    2015             : //      - uses a lot of intermediate memory, could cache poorly

    4887             : //    simple implementation
